# Ninereeds Grounded Stories — Story List
# Format: STORY / CLUSTER / LOCATION / SEASON / CHARACTERS / KEY WORDS / SEED
# Characters: E=Emma  T=Taro  G=Gran  B=Biscuit  L=Bello
# Locations: see world_bible.md — 12 locations now defined
# ------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#
# Extended metadata fields (stories 31+):
#   ARITHMETIC     — arithmetic fact being grounded (stories 31–48 and 151+)
#   ANSWER         — correct answer, hardcoded
#   STATES         — who says the arithmetic and how
#   COUNTS         — who counts aloud and what they say
#   PARAPHRASE     — alternate phrasing for the same fact
#   SPATIAL_CONCEPT — spatial relationship being grounded (stories 71–90)
#   TEMPORAL_RELATION — temporal concept being grounded (stories 91–110)
#   CAUSE_EFFECT   — causal chain being grounded (stories 111–130)
#   OBSERVATION_STATE — what changes depending on conditions or position
#   NOTES          — generation notes for any story
# ------------------------------------------------------------------------------

STORY: 01
CLUSTER: oak tree (autumn)
LOCATION: The Oak
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E T B
KEY WORDS: acorn, squirrel, branch, bark, root, leaf, seed, hole, nut, crack, climb, carry, bury, drop
SEED: Biscuit finds the squirrel's hole at the base of the oak. Taro climbs the low branch. An acorn drops. Emma picks it up — it fits in her palm, small and round and brown, with a rough cap.

STORY: 02
CLUSTER: autumn leaves
LOCATION: The Oak + Gran's field
SEASON: late autumn
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: leaf, red, yellow, brown, rake, pile, crunch, sweep, fall, wind, acorn, branch, bare
SEED: Gran is raking. The children jump in the pile. The oak is almost bare. One last leaf lets go and spins down.

STORY: 03
CLUSTER: oak in snow
LOCATION: The Oak
SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E T B
KEY WORDS: snow, bare, branch, frost, tracks, cold, hole, search, buried, white, quiet, footprint
SEED: Fresh snow. The squirrel tracks lead to the oak and stop at the hole. Biscuit circles the roots, sniffing. The low branch has a ridge of snow along its top.

STORY: 04
CLUSTER: bird's nest
LOCATION: The Oak (upper fork)
SEASON: spring
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: nest, egg, twig, feather, beak, hatch, feed, worm, chirp, branch, careful, high
SEED: Gran points out the nest in the oak's upper fork — too high to reach but close enough to see. Three pale blue eggs. Later in the week, there is sound from it.

STORY: 05
CLUSTER: rainy day
LOCATION: Meadow path + The Oak (shelter)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T B
KEY WORDS: rain, puddle, mud, drip, splash, cloud, storm, umbrella, boot, soak, stream, shelter, run
SEED: The rain starts before they reach the oak. They run for it. Biscuit does not run — he puts his nose up and lets the rain hit his face. By the time they reach the tree they are already wet.

STORY: 06
CLUSTER: garden (morning)
LOCATION: Gran's garden
SEASON: spring/summer
CHARACTERS: E G B
KEY WORDS: soil, seed, plant, water, dig, trowel, row, press, cover, dew, slug, worm, smell, earth
SEED: Gran is planting seeds before it gets hot. Emma is given a row to do herself. The soil is dark and cool and smells of something deep. Biscuit keeps digging in the wrong place.

STORY: 07
CLUSTER: garden (in bloom)
LOCATION: Gran's garden
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T G B
KEY WORDS: flower, bee, bloom, petal, stem, butterfly, smell, colour, warm, hover, land, buzz
SEED: The garden is loud with bees. A butterfly lands on Taro's arm and stays. Gran deadheads the roses — pulls the brown ones off and drops them in her apron pocket.

STORY: 08
CLUSTER: apple orchard
LOCATION: Gran's garden (apple tree)
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: apple, ripe, red, branch, twist, twist off, thud, basket, core, seed, ladder, reach, weight
SEED: The apple tree is heavy — branches bent with fruit. Gran holds the ladder. Taro reaches for the highest ones. Emma picks up the windfalls from the ground.

STORY: 09
CLUSTER: kitchen cooking
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen
SEASON: autumn/winter
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: pot, onion, garlic, soup, boil, stir, chop, steam, ladle, bowl, taste, salt, smell, hot, wooden spoon
SEED: Gran is making soup. Emma stands on a chair to reach the counter and is given the wooden spoon. The onions make her eyes water. Gran tastes it, adds something, tells her to stir again.

STORY: 10
CLUSTER: baking
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: flour, butter, sugar, egg, bowl, mix, knead, dough, oven, warm, smell, pull out, cool, taste, cookie
SEED: The kitchen smells of warm butter. Taro is in charge of mixing. Emma shapes the cookies — some round, some not. They wait by the oven. Gran tells them to stop opening it.

STORY: 11
CLUSTER: morning routine
LOCATION: Gran's house
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: wake, yawn, stretch, cold floor, wash, towel, mirror, dress, breakfast, stairs, light, early
SEED: The floor is cold. Emma can hear Gran already in the kitchen. Taro is still in bed. She pulls on her socks standing up, one foot at a time, and goes downstairs.

STORY: 12
CLUSTER: getting dressed (outdoor)
LOCATION: Gran's house (doorway)
SEASON: winter/autumn
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: coat, sock, boot, button, zip, sleeve, pocket, scarf, glove, muddy, wet, peel off, hang up
SEED: Gran at the door with coats. Taro can't find his left glove. Emma's boot zipper is stuck. They get out eventually. When they come back they are muddy from the knees down.

STORY: 13
CLUSTER: bedtime
LOCATION: Gran's house (bedroom)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: lamp, blanket, pillow, yawn, moon, shadow, whisper, dark, quiet, sleepy, curl up, close, dim
SEED: The lamp is low. The moon is through the curtain gap. Gran whispers something Emma can't quite hear before she goes. Emma listens to the house settle.

STORY: 14
CLUSTER: rainy window
LOCATION: Gran's house (sitting room)
SEASON: autumn/winter
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: window, rain, drop, trace, glass, curtain, reflection, inside, cosy, tea, book, outside, grey
SEED: Taro traces the path of a raindrop with his finger, following it down the glass. Gran is reading. The garden outside is blurred and grey.

STORY: 15
CLUSTER: winter evening
LOCATION: Gran's house (sitting room)
SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: fire, log, flame, candle, warmth, crackle, ash, ember, shadow, glow, fade, lap, quiet, dark
SEED: The fire has been going all day. The logs are nearly ash. Gran puts one more on before bed. The shadow of the flame moves on the ceiling.

STORY: 16
CLUSTER: pond life
LOCATION: The Pond
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T B
KEY WORDS: frog, lily, ripple, duck, dragonfly, reed, mud, splash, wade, catch, reflection, still, water, flat stone
SEED: The pond is still enough to see the sky in it. A frog drops from a lily pad before Emma can get close. Biscuit wades in up to his belly and stands there looking pleased.

STORY: 17
CLUSTER: fishing
LOCATION: The Pond
SEASON: summer/autumn
CHARACTERS: T G
KEY WORDS: rod, hook, line, bait, worm, cast, wait, tug, pull, catch, release, bank, bucket, patience, ripple
SEED: Gran shows Taro how to cast. They wait a long time. When something finally pulls, Taro stands up too fast and nearly falls in.

STORY: 18
CLUSTER: meadow / butterfly
LOCATION: Meadow path
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: grass, butterfly, flower, dandelion, nectar, wing, float, land, blow, seed, caterpillar, meadow, warm
SEED: They are supposed to be going to the pond. They get distracted. Emma blows a dandelion clock. Taro finds a caterpillar on a leaf and carries it very carefully to a better plant.

STORY: 19
CLUSTER: dog walk
LOCATION: Meadow path
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: T B
KEY WORDS: lead, sniff, pull, stick, fetch, bark, roll, puddle, pant, bound, ahead, back, ahead, run
SEED: Biscuit finds a smell under a hedge and will not leave it. Taro waits. Then Biscuit spots something and runs and the lead goes taut and Taro runs too whether he means to or not.

STORY: 20
CLUSTER: body and touch
LOCATION: Meadow path (fall and examination)
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: hand, finger, palm, knee, elbow, scratch, scrape, mud, sting, cold water, feel, hold, press
SEED: Taro falls on the path — palms and one knee. Emma looks at it seriously. They find the stream and he holds his hands in the cold water.

STORY: 21
CLUSTER: playground
LOCATION: Schoolyard
SEASON: spring/summer
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: swing, push, high, jump off, slide, rope, climb, fall, scratch, laugh, sand, bench, chase, catch
SEED: Emma jumps off the swing at the highest point — lands badly but gets up. Taro watches from the top of the climbing frame. Neither will admit they were scared.

STORY: 22
CLUSTER: schoolyard (social)
LOCATION: Schoolyard
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: bag, bench, gate, bell, line, share, borrow, drop, pick up, pocket, lend, forget, find
SEED: Emma drops her pencil through the grate. Taro has a spare. She will give it back. The bell goes before they can sort it out properly.

STORY: 23
CLUSTER: picnic
LOCATION: Meadow (by the pond)
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T G B
KEY WORDS: basket, blanket, bread, cheese, berry, bottle, cup, ant, crumb, spill, unpack, spread, pour, pack
SEED: Gran unpacks the basket. An ant finds the cheese before anyone does. Biscuit sits so close and so hopefully that Gran gives him the end of the bread.

STORY: 24
CLUSTER: birthday
LOCATION: Gran's house (kitchen + garden)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: cake, candle, blow, wish, gift, ribbon, wrap, open, surprise, clap, song, icing, count
SEED: Eight candles. Taro counts them to make sure. Emma blows and one stays lit. Gran says you have to try again. Emma wishes the same wish both times.

STORY: 25
CLUSTER: camping
LOCATION: Gran's field (overnight)
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T G B
KEY WORDS: tent, peg, mallet, pole, lantern, star, fire, log, roast, dark, shadow, night sound, damp, morning
SEED: The tent goes up crooked. Gran does not fix it. In the dark, sounds from the field are louder than they are in the day — rustling, something moving through grass. Biscuit sleeps across the door.

STORY: 26
CLUSTER: farm animals (neighbour's farm)
LOCATION: Field + farm edge (near meadow path)
SEASON: spring
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: sheep, lamb, wool, fence, hay, gate, feed, smell, low, warm, breath, pen, bucket, barn
SEED: The lambs were born last week. Gran knows the farmer. They are let in through the gate. The lambs are smaller than Biscuit and have the same uncertain legs.

STORY: 27
CLUSTER: farm field (harvest)
LOCATION: Field beside The Oak
SEASON: late summer
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: wheat, ripe, tall, cut, fall, bundle, carry, field, dusty, chaff, warm, scratch, heavy, barn
SEED: The field is being cut. The children stand at the edge and watch. Gran explains that by the time the cutter reaches the middle, all the animals that were hiding in the wheat will have to run.

STORY: 28
CLUSTER: building / making
LOCATION: Gran's garden shed
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: T G
KEY WORDS: plank, nail, hammer, saw, measure, mark, hold still, wobble, bang thumb, fix, straight, try again
SEED: Taro is building a small shelf for his room — or trying to. Gran hands him things when he needs them and does not take over. It wobbles. She shows him the problem. He fixes it.

STORY: 29
CLUSTER: snowy day
LOCATION: Gran's field + The Oak
SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E T B G
KEY WORDS: snow, boot, thick, sink, cold, sled, hill, fast, fall, pack, throw, red cheeks, breath, melt, drip
SEED: The hill behind the field is steep enough to sled. One run each, then they have to carry the sled back up. Biscuit runs alongside and barks at the sled the whole way down.

STORY: 30
CLUSTER: mountain / hill (day trip)
LOCATION: The hill above the valley (day trip, visible from The Oak)
SEASON: late summer
CHARACTERS: E T G B
KEY WORDS: trail, climb, rock, loose, careful, rest, high, view, wind, valley, far, small, tired, down
SEED: From the top they can see Gran's cottage. It is very small. Emma finds the oak tree — a dark shape in the patchwork of fields. Taro is already starting down.

# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# ARITHMETIC STATE-CHANGE STORIES (31–48)
# Extended fields:
#   ARITHMETIC  — the fact being grounded (e.g. 2+2=4)
#   ANSWER      — the correct answer in words (hardcoded; DeepSeek must not change this)
#   STATES      — which character says the arithmetic aloud, and in what form
#   COUNTS      — which character counts aloud, and the counting line
#   PARAPHRASE  — alternate phrasing used for the same fact in the same story
#   NOTES       — generation notes
# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

STORY: 31
CLUSTER: apples for the cake (2+2=4)
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen + garden + market
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E T G B
KEY WORDS: apple, basket, tree, counter, count, enough, cake, market, carry, line up
ARITHMETIC: 2+2=4
ANSWER: four
STATES: Taro says "Two plus two equals four." before going to the market.
COUNTS: Emma lines the apples up on the counter and counts aloud: "One, two, three, four."
PARAPHRASE: After counting, Emma says "two and two is four" or "Taro was right".
SEED: Gran needs four apples for the cake. Emma picks two from the garden tree. Not enough. Taro takes the basket to the market with Biscuit. When he comes back Emma lines them up on the counter and counts.

STORY: 32
CLUSTER: eggs for breakfast (1+2=3)
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen + garden henhouse + shed
SEASON: spring
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: egg, henhouse, shelf, basket, bowl, crack, count, breakfast, enough
ARITHMETIC: 1+2=3
ANSWER: three
STATES: Taro says "One and two is three. That is enough."
COUNTS: Gran sets them on the table one at a time: "One. Two. Three."
PARAPHRASE: Taro says "one and two" rather than "one plus two".
SEED: Gran needs three eggs for breakfast. Emma finds one in the henhouse. Taro remembers there were some in the shed. They check. Gran counts what is on the table.

STORY: 33
CLUSTER: logs for the fire A — Emma then Taro (1+3=4)
LOCATION: Gran's house fireplace + woodpile
SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: log, woodpile, carry, stack, fireplace, cold, enough, count, evening
ARITHMETIC: 1+3=4
ANSWER: four
STATES: Gran says "One and three makes four. That will do."
COUNTS: Gran touches each log: "One, two, three, four."
PARAPHRASE: Gran says "makes four" rather than "equals four" or "is four".
SEED: The fire needs more logs for the evening. Emma brings one from the woodpile. Gran says it is not enough. Taro goes back and comes back with three more stacked in his arms. Gran counts them.

STORY: 34
CLUSTER: logs for the fire B — Taro then Emma (3+1=4, commutativity pair with 33)
LOCATION: Gran's house fireplace + woodpile
SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: log, woodpile, carry, stack, fireplace, count, same, again, enough
ARITHMETIC: 3+1=4
ANSWER: four
STATES: Taro says "Three and one — same as before. Four."
COUNTS: Taro counts: "One, two, three — and Emma's makes four."
PARAPHRASE: Taro says "same as before" — explicitly noting commutativity.
NOTES: Commutativity pair with story 33. Same location, same season, same goal. The count comes out the same even though the order is reversed.
SEED: This time Taro goes first and carries three. Still one short. Emma brings the last one. Taro counts. It comes out the same as last time.

STORY: 35
CLUSTER: berries for jam A — Emma then Taro (2+3=5)
LOCATION: Gran's garden + hedgerow by the gate
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: berry, bush, hedgerow, handful, bowl, purple, fingers, jam, count, pour
ARITHMETIC: 2+3=5
ANSWER: five
STATES: Emma says "Two and three — that is five."
COUNTS: Gran tips them into the bowl and counts: "One, two, three, four, five."
PARAPHRASE: Emma says "two and three" rather than "two plus three".
SEED: The jam needs berries. Emma picks the ones in the garden. Not enough. Taro knows there are more at the hedgerow by the gate. They come back with purple fingers. Gran counts them into the bowl.

STORY: 36
CLUSTER: berries for jam B — Taro then Emma (3+2=5, commutativity pair with 35)
LOCATION: Gran's garden + hedgerow by the gate
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: berry, bush, hedgerow, handful, bowl, purple, jam, count, same, pour
ARITHMETIC: 3+2=5
ANSWER: five
STATES: Gran says "Three and two, five. Same as the other way."
COUNTS: Gran: "One, two, three, four, five. Yes."
PARAPHRASE: Gran says "same as the other way" — explicitly noting commutativity.
NOTES: Commutativity pair with story 35. Same location, same season, same goal.
SEED: This time Taro picks first. Still not quite enough. Emma adds the last two from the garden. Gran tips them all into the bowl and counts. The number comes out the same.

STORY: 37
CLUSTER: empty basket — apple tree (0+3=3)
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen + garden apple tree
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: basket, empty, apple, tree, branch, low, count, three, nothing, before
ARITHMETIC: 0+3=3
ANSWER: three
STATES: Gran says "Zero plus three is three. That is what I need."
COUNTS: Emma sets them on the table one at a time: "One. Two. Three."
PARAPHRASE: Gran may say "nothing in the basket, three from the tree — three."
NOTES: Zero identity. The basket is explicitly empty before Emma picks. Gran names zero as a quantity.
SEED: Gran opens the kitchen basket — it is empty. She asks Emma to check the apple tree. Emma comes back with three apples and puts them on the table one at a time.

STORY: 38
CLUSTER: market closed — apples already there (3+0=3)
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen + meadow path
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: apple, bowl, market, closed, empty hands, count, same, nothing, still
ARITHMETIC: 3+0=3
ANSWER: three
STATES: Taro says "Three and nothing is still three."
COUNTS: Emma: "One, two, three. Same as before."
PARAPHRASE: Taro says "three and nothing" rather than "three plus zero".
NOTES: Zero identity — adding zero leaves the count unchanged. Taro returns empty-handed; the number in the bowl does not change.
SEED: Taro was sent to get more apples but the market stall was shut. He comes back with nothing. Emma counts what Gran already has in the bowl.

STORY: 39
CLUSTER: Emma eats the snack apples (4−2=2)
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: apple, bowl, eat, snack, count, left, fewer, take away, not enough
ARITHMETIC: 4-2=2
ANSWER: two
STATES: Taro says "Four, take away two — two left. We ate too many."
COUNTS: Taro: "One, two. Only two."
PARAPHRASE: Taro says "take away" rather than "minus".
NOTES: Subtraction as depletion. Gran had set the apples aside for something. Emma and Taro each eat one. Taro realises they will need to get more.
SEED: Gran had put four apples aside. Emma took one and Taro took one. When Gran comes back, Taro counts what is left in the bowl.

STORY: 40
CLUSTER: candles at morning (5−3=2)
LOCATION: Gran's sitting room
SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: candle, burned, wax, wick, morning, count, left, gone, two, five
ARITHMETIC: 5-3=2
ANSWER: two
STATES: Gran says "Five candles, three burned out — two left."
COUNTS: Emma: "One, two. That is all."
PARAPHRASE: Gran says "burned out" as the depletion verb, not "subtracted" or "minus".
SEED: Five candles had been lit the evening before. In the morning Emma could see that three of them had burned to nothing. Gran counted what remained without looking.

STORY: 41
CLUSTER: egg for Biscuit (4−1=3)
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G B
KEY WORDS: egg, bowl, crack, biscuit, cake, batter, count, left, one for, three for
ARITHMETIC: 4-1=3
ANSWER: three
STATES: Gran says "One for Biscuit, three for the cake. Four take one is three."
COUNTS: Taro: "One, two, three. Yes, still enough."
PARAPHRASE: Gran says "four take one" rather than "four minus one".
SEED: Gran cracks one egg into Biscuit's breakfast bowl before she starts the cake batter. Biscuit eats it before Gran has put the shell down. Taro counts what is left in the bowl for the batter.

STORY: 42
CLUSTER: bowls for the table — deficit framing (need 4, have 1, get 3 more → 1+3=4)
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: bowl, shelf, cupboard, table, place, count, enough, four, one, three
ARITHMETIC: 1+3=4
ANSWER: four
STATES: Taro says "One from the shelf, three from the cupboard. One and three is four."
COUNTS: Emma places one bowl at each seat: "One, two, three, four. Just right."
PARAPHRASE: Emma says "just right" — the goal met exactly, not a numerical restatement.
NOTES: Deficit framing: the goal (4 bowls) is known first; the gap drives the action.
SEED: Gran needs four bowls for the table. Emma finds one on the shelf. Three more are needed. Taro opens the cupboard.

STORY: 43
CLUSTER: logs for the night — deficit framing (need 5, have 2, get 3 more → 2+3=5)
LOCATION: Gran's sitting room + woodpile
SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: log, basket, count, night, enough, cold, trip, woodpile, five, two, three
ARITHMETIC: 2+3=5
ANSWER: five
STATES: Taro says "Two we have, three more I will get. Two plus three is five."
COUNTS: Gran stacks them and counts: "One, two, three, four, five. That should last."
PARAPHRASE: Gran says "that should last" — verification is practical, not purely numerical.
NOTES: Deficit framing: Gran names the goal (5 logs) before anyone counts what is there.
SEED: Gran counts the logs in the basket. Not enough for the whole night. Emma counts two. Three more are needed. Taro goes out into the cold.

STORY: 44
CLUSTER: fish for supper — deficit framing (need 3, have 0, catch 3)
LOCATION: The Pond
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: T G B
KEY WORDS: fish, rod, line, catch, bucket, count, supper, none, pond, three, Biscuit
ARITHMETIC: 0+3=3
ANSWER: three
STATES: Taro says "None to start with, three now. That is what Gran needs."
COUNTS: Taro counts before heading home: "One, two, three. Right."
PARAPHRASE: Taro says "none to start with" — zero as "none" rather than as a number name.
NOTES: Zero-identity via deficit framing. Biscuit sits unusually still and watches the line.
SEED: Gran needs fish for supper and there are none in the house. Taro takes the rod down to the pond. Biscuit sits very still for once and watches the line.

STORY: 45
CLUSTER: no pears on the tree (zero as answer to "how many")
LOCATION: Gran's garden (pear tree)
SEASON: late summer
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: pear, tree, branch, look, count, none, zero, answer, number, check
ARITHMETIC: zero (the answer to "how many" is zero)
ANSWER: zero
STATES: Emma says "None. Zero pears." Gran says "Zero is the answer. Zero is a number."
COUNTS: Emma scans each branch carefully, finding nothing.
PARAPHRASE: Emma says "none" first, then Gran names it "zero".
NOTES: Zero as a valid answer — not a failure or absence, but a quantity with a name.
SEED: Gran sends Emma to check the pear tree and count how many are ready. Emma goes along every branch carefully. She comes back to the kitchen.

STORY: 46
CLUSTER: empty coat pocket (3+0=3 — zero as addend)
LOCATION: Gran's house doorway
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: T G
KEY WORDS: pocket, coat, walnut, bowl, count, empty, nothing, same, still, three
ARITHMETIC: 3+0=3
ANSWER: three
STATES: Gran says "Three and nothing is still three. It is enough."
COUNTS: Gran: "One, two, three. Same as before."
PARAPHRASE: Gran says "three and nothing" — zero as "nothing" rather than as a number name.
NOTES: Parallel to story 38 (market closed) but pocket framing. Zero as addend leaves quantity unchanged.
SEED: Taro comes in from the meadow. Gran asks if he found any walnuts on the way. He checks both coat pockets. Gran already has some in the bowl.

STORY: 47
CLUSTER: school lesson — arithmetic presentation (2+2=4, "is" and "equals" bridged)
LOCATION: Schoolroom (inside the school at the end of the meadow path)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E
KEY WORDS: teacher, slate, board, chalk, write, answer, correct, number, symbols, lesson
ARITHMETIC: 2+2=4
ANSWER: four
STATES: Emma says "Two plus two is four." The teacher says "Correct — two plus two equals four." and writes 2+2=4 on the slate.
COUNTS: (not applicable — direct retrieval, no physical objects to count)
PARAPHRASE: "is" (Emma) → "equals" (teacher) → 2+2=4 (written symbol). All three are shown as the same fact.
NOTES: Presentation story. Explicitly teaches that "is", "equals", and the written symbol are three forms of the same arithmetic fact. Should appear early in training relative to the other arithmetic stories. The teacher is unnamed — just "the teacher".
SEED: The teacher writes a number on the board and asks Emma the answer. Emma says it right. The teacher says it back a different way and writes it as symbols on the slate.

STORY: 48
CLUSTER: Bello arrives — a second dog (1+1=2)
LOCATION: Gran's house + garden
SEASON: spring
CHARACTERS: E T G B
KEY WORDS: dog, new, arrive, small, sniff, two, one, before, now, Bello, run, chase, together
ARITHMETIC: 1+1=2
ANSWER: two
STATES: Emma says "We had one dog. Now we have two."
COUNTS: Gran smiles: "One dog, two dogs." She counts on her fingers.
PARAPHRASE: Emma says "one and one" or Taro says "twice the trouble" — the fact is also demonstrated by two dogs running in the garden.
NOTES: Introduces Bello as a new character. 1+1=2 is the simplest addition fact, grounded in a real event. Biscuit reacts to Bello — sniffs, circles, uncertain. By the end they are running together.
SEED: A small dog arrives at Gran's cottage — Bello. Biscuit sniffs at him from a distance. By the end of the afternoon they are both in the garden. Emma counts them.

# BLOCK 1: NEW LOCATIONS + WORLDBUILDING (49–70)
# These stories establish the expanded world. Each introduces a location,
# a sensory register, or a persistent fact that later stories will reference.
# No new metadata fields yet — these are pure grounded narrative.

STORY: 49
CLUSTER: bench by the pond (first use)
LOCATION: The Pond (bench + flat stone)
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: bench, flat stone, still, reflect, fish, shadow, watch, disappear, quiet, willow, afternoon
OBSERVATION_STATE: Fish visible from flat stone when water is still and no shadow crosses; gone the moment a shadow falls.
SEED: Gran is on the bench. Emma is on the flat stone, close to the water. She can see fish — small and slow near the bottom. She shifts her weight and her shadow crosses the water. The fish are gone.
NOTES: Establishes the pond bench and the observation-dependent fish state. Gran does not explain why the fish disappeared. Emma works it out herself.

STORY: 50
CLUSTER: fish at the pond — morning vs. afternoon
LOCATION: The Pond (flat stone)
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: fish, surface, shadow, light, angle, morning, afternoon, still, visible, gone, cloud, wait
OBSERVATION_STATE: Fish closer to the surface in early morning; deeper by afternoon. A cloud passing makes them disappear briefly.
SEED: They come to the pond in the morning and again after lunch. Emma thinks there are more fish in the morning. Taro says it's the same fish. Neither can prove it.
NOTES: Same location, different time of day — establishes temporal change within a single day. No resolution; the question stays open.

STORY: 51
CLUSTER: Biscuit jumps in the pond
LOCATION: The Pond
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T B
KEY WORDS: run, jump, splash, soak, shake, spray, bank, soaked, shake off, laugh, wet, shore, wade
SEED: Biscuit is running at full speed along the bank. He does not slow down. Emma just has time to step back. He hits the water and disappears for a moment under the splash, then comes up swimming, ears flat, looking very pleased. He climbs out and shakes.
NOTES: Pure kinetic scene. Uses Biscuit's established character — impulsive, physical, unembarrassed. Good for movement vocabulary and water physics.

STORY: 52
CLUSTER: feeding the ducks
LOCATION: The Pond (bank + bench)
SEASON: spring
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: duck, bread, crust, tear, throw, scramble, bill, feather, ripple, near, close, trust, crumble
SEED: Gran tears bread into small pieces and gives them to Emma. Emma throws pieces toward the ducks. The ducks come closer with each throw. By the last piece they are almost near enough to touch. Gran says not to.
NOTES: Gradual approach — good for near/far and trust/caution. Gran's "not to" is delivered while still watching the ducks, not as a lecture.

STORY: 53
CLUSTER: egg morning
LOCATION: Gran's garden (henhouse)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: henhouse, hen, feather, straw, warm, brown, egg, basket, quiet, morning, careful, nest, collect
SEED: Emma carries the small basket. The henhouse smells of straw and warm feathers. One hen is still on her nest and will not move. Emma reaches under her very carefully and finds two eggs. The third is on the floor in the corner, unbroken.
NOTES: Establishes the henhouse. Three eggs, but reached by different paths — good for subtle counting context. The reluctant hen is character detail; do not resolve it neatly.

STORY: 54
CLUSTER: the one ripe week (pear tree)
LOCATION: Gran's garden (pear tree, east wall)
SEASON: early autumn
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: pear, hard, soft, smell, wall, press, thumb, ready, wait, fall, too soon, right, window
SEED: Gran checks the pear tree every morning for a few days — a slight press of her thumb, a sniff. Emma watches. Then one morning Gran says they're ready. They pick everything they can reach. Two days later, the ones they missed have fallen.
NOTES: Establishes the pear tree's single ripe week — a temporal window that cannot be recaptured. Teaches: readiness is a state, not a permanent property. Gran's thumb-press is the instrument.

STORY: 55
CLUSTER: compost corner
LOCATION: Gran's garden (compost corner behind shed)
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E G B
KEY WORDS: lid, stick, steam, warm, dark, earthworm, scraps, carrot, peel, smell, layer, turn, soil, rot
SEED: Gran lifts the compost lid with a stick. Steam comes up. Emma looks in — dark material, the smell of something working. Gran points to an earthworm threading through it. Biscuit pushes his nose toward the opening and sneezes.
NOTES: Establishes the compost corner and the transformation process. Steam on a cold morning is the key sensory detail. No explanation needed — Gran shows, Emma observes.

STORY: 56
CLUSTER: herb harvest
LOCATION: Gran's garden (herb trough by kitchen door)

NOTES: Establishes the herb trough. The smell-before-name approach is deliberate — builds sensory vocabulary without labelling. Which herb is grey-green is intentionally unspecified.

STORY: 57

NOTES: First use of the village lane. Establishes the topology — chimney + oak visible from the top, the baker's smell as the arrival signal. Taro steps in the puddle as character consistency.

STORY: 58

SEED: The bell above the door rings when they go in. The smell is even stronger inside. Gran asks for a loaf. The baker wraps it in paper and the weight of it goes into Emma's arms to carry home.
NOTES: First use of the baker. Establishes physical details: the bell, the paper wrapping, the warm weight. The loaf is Emma's to carry — gives her a bodily relationship to the bread before it becomes food.

STORY: 59

STORY: 60
CLUSTER: Gran on the bench (garden)

SEED: Gran is on the bench in the afternoon sun with a bowl of beans to top and tail. Biscuit is asleep at her feet in the warm patch. The garden is quiet except for the bees. Gran works without hurrying. Biscuit twitches once and goes still.
NOTES: No children — a rare quiet scene with Gran and Biscuit alone. Establishes the garden bench as Gran's place. The afternoon sun, the bean-snapping sound, the sleeping dog build a persistent image.

STORY: 61
CLUSTER: upstairs at night (rain on the tiles)
LOCATION: Gran's house (loft bedroom)
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: rain, tiles, close, loud, skylight, dark, dry, warm, blanket, listen, settle, creak, outside, in
SEED: The rain starts after they are in bed. On the tiles it is very close and very loud — not like rain heard from downstairs. Emma lies still and listens. Taro is already asleep. The rain goes on. The room is dry and warm; the rain is just on the other side of the tiles.
NOTES: Establishes the upstairs and the close sound of rain on the roof. The distinction between inside/outside — warm and dry vs. wet and loud — is the core sensation. No plot required.

STORY: 62
CLUSTER: morning skylight

KEY WORDS: skylight, stick, light, early, blue, open, cool, air, smell, morning, dew, grass, woken, first
SEED: The light wakes Emma before anyone else. She opens the skylight with the stick — it takes two tries. Cool air comes in, smelling of grass and something she can't name. She can see a strip of blue sky and, at the edge, the tip of the apple tree.
NOTES: The skylight gives the room a connection to the outside. The smell of morning comes in before anything is visible. The apple tree's tip in the frame connects upstairs to the garden.

STORY: 63

SEED: They take a jar of tadpoles from the pond to school. Taro carries it very carefully all the way along the meadow path. In the classroom it goes on the nature table by the window. The whole class comes to look.
NOTES: Connects the pond to the classroom — topology in action. The careful carrying is character consistency for Taro (he carried the caterpillar carefully in story 18). The tadpoles will be returned; this is implied, not stated.

STORY: 64
CLUSTER: inside the classroom

CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: desk, chalk, board, radiator, click, smell, wood, initial, carve, coat hook, corridor, cold outside, warm in
SEED: The classroom is warm from the radiator. Through the tall windows the yard is grey and cold. Emma runs her finger along the carved initials on her desk — letters that someone put there long before her. The teacher writes something on the board and the chalk squeaks.
NOTES: Establishes the classroom sensory register. The carved initials are a detail that implies history — other children, other years — without stating it. Connects the warmth inside to the cold yard outside.

STORY: 65
CLUSTER: Emma sick on the sofa
LOCATION: Gran's house (sitting room)

CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: sofa, blanket, hot, throat, swallow, curtains, dim, clock, quiet, soup, bowl, low table, still
SEED: Emma is on the sofa under the brown blanket. Her throat makes swallowing something she is aware of. The curtains are half drawn. The clock is louder than usual, or she is hearing it more. Gran brings soup and puts it on the low table without saying anything about it.
NOTES: First sick-on-sofa story. Use the sensory register from the world bible entry: not "Emma was ill," but the felt quality of it. Gran's soup delivered silently is important — no fussing, no instructions.

STORY: 66
CLUSTER: the day after sick
LOCATION: Gran's house (sitting room → garden)
SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: better, light, different, cold, outside, window, sharp, hunger, first day, stand, slow, garden, step
SEED: Emma wakes up knowing she is better. The room looks different — sharper, more itself. She is hungry in a way she wasn't yesterday. Gran lets her come downstairs. By afternoon she is at the kitchen window looking at the garden, wanting to go out.
NOTES: Recovery as a state change — the world returning to normal, but slightly different. The sharpness of perception after illness. Hunger as a signal of health. Not back to full activity — standing at the window is enough.

STORY: 67

SEED: Taro's stomach ache comes in waves. Between waves he is almost alright; during a wave he cannot do anything except be still. Gran gives him water in small amounts. He lies very carefully on his side. Eventually the waves come further apart.
NOTES: Different sensory register to Emma's sick story — stomach vs. throat. The wave pattern is important: not constant, but rhythmic. Gran's approach is the same: minimal fuss, practical, present.

The metal table is cold; Biscuit stands on it with the expression of someone enduring something. The needle is quick. He gets a treat from the vet's coat pocket.

STORY: 70

NOTES: Establishes Bello at the vet and the vet's approach to nervous animals. The arc is: afraid → enduring → calm. Emma carrying him in and out is character detail — she is gentle with small things.

STORY: 71
CLUSTER: above and below at the oak
LOCATION: The Oak
SEASON: spring
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: nest, above, roots, below, branch, middle, up, down, between, high, low, ground
SPATIAL_CONCEPT: above / below / between — three vertical layers in one place
SEED: Gran points to the robin's nest high in the fork. The squirrel's hole is at the base of the roots, in the ground. The children are in between — standing on the roots, looking up at the nest.
NOTES: Three vertical layers: nest above, squirrel hole below, children in the middle. No explanation — Gran just points up, then down.

STORY: 72
CLUSTER: above and below at the pond
LOCATION: The Pond (flat stone)
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: dragonfly, surface, fish, below, above, sky, reflection, skim, deep, shallow, layer, middle
SPATIAL_CONCEPT: above the surface / at the surface / below the surface — three layers visible at once
SEED: A dragonfly skims above the water. The surface reflects the sky. Below it Emma can see fish moving slowly near the bottom. Three things at once, in the same column of space.
NOTES: The reflection is important — the sky appears both above and in the water. Emma sees it twice.

STORY: 73

SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: apple, cut, core, pip, seed, inside, outside, skin, flesh, white, brown, star, knife, half
SPATIAL_CONCEPT: inside / outside — what is contained vs. what is visible
SEED: Gran cuts an apple in half. The inside is white and cool. There are five pips arranged in a star around the core. Emma did not know they were there until the cut.
NOTES: Hidden interior revealed by action. The pip arrangement is a detail worth including — it implies structure even before it is visible.

STORY: 74

SEASON: any

SPATIAL_CONCEPT: through — sound passes through solid barriers, muffled but present
SEED: Emma can hear Gran in the kitchen below — a clatter, a word, something moving. Not clear enough to make out, but definitely there. She listens at the floor. When the kitchen door opens, the sounds become sharper.
NOTES: Sound as evidence of location. Gran is below, unseen but heard. The door opening changes the path of the sound.

STORY: 75

SPATIAL_CONCEPT: near / far — the same sound changes with distance
SEED: From far down the meadow path, the school bell is barely there — a faint note on the still air. They run. By the time they reach the gate, it is loud and urgent. The same bell, the same note — just closer.

STORY: 76

STORY: 77

STORY: 78

STORY: 79

STORY: 80

SPATIAL_CONCEPT: against — something can be shaped by and bound to a surface

STORY: 81

SEED: The rain starts. They run for the oak. Under the canopy it is nearly dry — the leaves catch most of it. But at the edge of the canopy, drops fall in a curtain. The dry patch is exactly the size of the tree's reach.
NOTES: The dry space is not infinite — it has edges. The canopy's reach defines the shelter. Moving to the edge of it changes what hits you.

STORY: 87

STORY: 89

STORY: 90

SPATIAL_CONCEPT: around a corner — what is hidden before and visible after a turn
SEED: Gran is ahead and turns the corner into the village street. From the lane, she disappears. Then Emma turns the corner and Gran is right there. The village opens up at the same moment.
NOTES: The corner creates a discontinuity in visibility. Something that existed but was invisible becomes visible at the turn. No drama required — it is an everyday spatial experience.

STORY: 91
CLUSTER: before and after the rain
LOCATION: Meadow path + Gran's garden
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E T G

TEMPORAL_RELATION: before / after — the same place has different states
SEED: Gran says: remember what the path looked like this morning. They go out after lunch. The path is different — puddles in the dip, mud at the edges. The same path. Just after rain.
NOTES: Gran's instruction to remember creates the before state actively. The after is observed together. No summary needed.

STORY: 92
CLUSTER: waiting for the bread
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: oven, wait, smell, time, yet, not yet, check, door, warm, rise, stay, patience, almost, done
TEMPORAL_RELATION: duration / not yet — something is happening but not complete
SEED: The bread is in the oven. It is not done yet. Gran says stop opening it. The smell gets stronger — that means it is getting closer. Taro opens it once anyway. Gran closes it again without saying anything.
NOTES: The intensifying smell is a temporal signal — the evidence that time is passing and the bread is changing. Taro's impatience is character consistency.

STORY: 93
CLUSTER: the seed is in (nothing visible yet)
LOCATION: Gran's garden (vegetable patch)
SEASON: spring
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: seed, soil, press, cover, water, wait, nothing, there, below, invisible, change, begin, now
TEMPORAL_RELATION: hidden transformation — something has started but cannot yet be observed
SEED: Emma presses the last seed into the soil and covers it. The row looks exactly like it did before. Gran says: it is already changing. Emma looks at the soil. Nothing is different yet.
NOTES: The transformation has begun but is invisible. Gran's assertion is taken on trust. This is the first story in the seed arc — the others follow.

STORY: 94
CLUSTER: the shoot appears
LOCATION: Gran's garden (vegetable patch)
SEASON: spring
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: shoot, pale, thin, soil, through, there, look, bent, week, later, same row, first, arrived
TEMPORAL_RELATION: delayed appearance — change was occurring before it became visible
SEED: Three weeks after the planting. Emma checks the row every few days. Then one morning: a pale thin shoot, bent like a hook, coming up through the soil. It was not there yesterday. Or maybe it was, just below.
NOTES: The "maybe it was, just below" is important — the shoot did not appear from nothing, it crossed the threshold of visibility. Emma's daily checking establishes the interval.

STORY: 95
CLUSTER: the full plant (seed arc complete)
LOCATION: Gran's garden (vegetable patch)
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: plant, green, tall, leaf, row, full, compare, remember, same, different, from, to, grew, now
TEMPORAL_RELATION: transformation complete — comparing current state to remembered past
SEED: The row is full now — tall green plants, leaves broad. Gran asks if Emma remembers what it looked like when they planted. Emma does. The row was bare soil. Now this. Same row.
NOTES: The arc closes: bare soil → invisible seed → shoot → full plant. The comparison is the lesson. No numbers or labels — just memory vs. observation.

STORY: 96
CLUSTER: morning vs. afternoon at the pond
LOCATION: The Pond
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: morning, afternoon, light, angle, shadow, fish, surface, different, same, time, change, return
TEMPORAL_RELATION: time of day changes what is seen at the same place
SEED: They come to the pond in the morning — still water, fish near the surface, the light flat. They come back after lunch. The light is different — harder, the shadow of the willow across the water. The fish are deeper.
NOTES: Same pond, two visits, different appearance. No one explains why. The children notice the difference without connecting it to time of day directly.

STORY: 97
CLUSTER: counting sleeps
LOCATION: Gran's house (bedroom + kitchen)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: sleeps, count, days, until, morning, fingers, before, how many, wait, anticipate, tomorrow, after
TEMPORAL_RELATION: counting intervals — duration expressed as a number of sleeps
SEED: Gran's birthday is in four days. Taro says: four sleeps. He holds up four fingers. Emma counts on her fingers too. At breakfast the next day, Taro holds up three fingers before he says anything else.
NOTES: Counting sleeps is a child's way of making duration concrete and countable. The reduction from four to three demonstrates that counting down is counting time passing.

STORY: 98
CLUSTER: the egg has not hatched yet

TEMPORAL_RELATION: anticipation of a known future event — the change will come but has not
SEED: The three eggs are still there. They have checked for four days. Gran says: it takes a few more days yet. Emma can see one egg from the ground if she stands at the right angle. Same as yesterday.
NOTES: The "same as yesterday" is the temporal content — no change observed, but that does not mean nothing is happening. See story 99 for the after.

STORY: 99
CLUSTER: the egg has hatched

SEED: The morning they find it, they hear the nest before they see it — a thin, fast sound. Something has changed. The eggs are gone. Gran says it happened in the night.
NOTES: Pair with story 98. The change happened when no one was watching. This is important: time passes whether observed or not. Absence from the scene does not pause it.

STORY: 101

SEED: Emma is looking at a windfall apple and remembers Gran said last week that the ones with a brown spot were already going soft inside. She checks the spot. Gran was right. She puts it in the keep pile or the compost pile accordingly.

STORY: 102

STORY: 103
CLUSTER: retracing steps to find the lost boot

TEMPORAL_RELATION: retracing in time and space — memory locates a lost object
SEED: Emma has one boot. The other one is somewhere. She tries to remember: when did she last have both? At the gate. Before that — the bench. She walks back. The boot is under the bench where she sat to tie it.
NOTES: Retracing is both temporal (when did I last have it?) and spatial (where was I then?). The two are inseparable in this story.

STORY: 104

SEED: The blackberries are red. Gran says: not yet. Emma checks them every few days on the way past. Red, then darker red, then a cluster that is almost black. Gran says: not yet. Then one day Gran says nothing and picks one.

STORY: 105

TEMPORAL_RELATION: the ready window — the moment of readiness, with urgency
SEED: They pick fast — Gran says the birds will get the rest if they wait. Emma's fingers are purple by the time the bowl is half full. The ones at the top were too high yesterday; today she can reach them.

STORY: 107

STORY: 108

STORY: 109

STORY: 110
CLUSTER: winter into spring at the oak
LOCATION: The Oak

KEY WORDS: bare, first, bud, small, green, appear, edge, branch, begin, winter, spring, signal, change
TEMPORAL_RELATION: the turning point between seasons — the first sign of change
SEED: The oak has been bare all winter. Emma and Gran walk past it on a cold morning in late February. Gran stops and points to one low branch. The first tiny buds — pale green, barely there, like small decisions.
NOTES: The signal of spring is noticed before spring has arrived. Gran's gesture makes Emma look where she would not have looked. "Like small decisions" — each bud is a small event that accumulates into spring.

# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# BLOCK 4: OBSERVATION AND CAUSE-EFFECT (111–130)
# Each story shows how one state produces another through physical causality.
# The cause-effect chain is never stated; it is observed.
# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

STORY: 111
CLUSTER: frost on the window
LOCATION: Gran's house (upstairs bedroom)
SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E
KEY WORDS: frost, glass, pattern, finger, melt, trace, cold, breath, fog, clear, spot, outside, white, lace
CAUSE_EFFECT: cold air on the outside of warm glass → frost crystals form; warmth from a finger → frost melts
SEED: Emma wakes to frost on the skylight glass — white patterns, branching like roots. She traces one with her finger. The frost melts exactly where she touched, leaving a clear spot. Her breath fogs the glass.
NOTES: Three causes in one small scene: cold → frost, warmth → melt, breath → fog. None are explained.

STORY: 112
CLUSTER: ice at the pond edge
LOCATION: The Pond
SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E T B
KEY WORDS: ice, edge, solid, middle, open, cold, thin, crack, careful, test, step, reed, frozen, clear
CAUSE_EFFECT: sustained cold → water freezes at the edges first (shallow); deeper centre stays open
SEED: The pond's edges are frozen — a thin shelf of ice over the reeds. The centre is still open water. Taro tests the ice with his boot. It holds for a moment, then cracks. Biscuit puts one paw on it and steps back.
NOTES: The partial freeze pattern (edges first) is the physical detail. The ice holds briefly — the thickness is marginal. Nobody falls in.

STORY: 113
CLUSTER: ice melts in the afternoon
LOCATION: The Pond
SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: sun, afternoon, drip, melt, edge, shrink, smaller, morning, same pond, warmer, gone, left
CAUSE_EFFECT: afternoon sun warms air and water → ice retreats from the outer edge inward
SEED: In the morning the ice shelf was wide. By afternoon it has retreated — the drip line is further in, the edges are slush. Gran says it is the afternoon sun. What was solid this morning is gone.
NOTES: Pair with story 112. The melting is a daytime reversal of the overnight freezing. The cause (afternoon sun) is named by Gran but not explained.

STORY: 114
CLUSTER: wet boots by the fire
LOCATION: Gran's house (fireplace + doorway)
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: wet, boot, fire, dry, morning, gone, steam, overnight, beside, warm, heat, leather, changed
CAUSE_EFFECT: wet boots placed near heat source overnight → dry by morning
SEED: They come in soaked. Gran puts the boots by the fire. In the morning Emma picks hers up — dry, stiff, warm. The fire has done it. The smell of drying leather is in the whole room.
NOTES: The transformation is invisible (it happened overnight) but the result is observable. The smell is the evidence of the process.

STORY: 115
CLUSTER: shadow direction — morning and afternoon
LOCATION: Gran's garden (stone or post that casts a shadow)
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: shadow, morning, direction, afternoon, moved, same post, different, sun, side, left, right, trace, time
CAUSE_EFFECT: sun moves across the sky → shadows rotate around objects through the day
SEED: In the morning the shadow of the gatestone points one way. Emma marks the tip with a stick in the soil. In the afternoon the shadow has turned — the tip is somewhere else. The stone has not moved.
NOTES: Emma marks the shadow tip at two times — the comparison is exact and personal. The cause (sun moving) is implied by the result. Gran may say a word but is not required.

STORY: 116
CLUSTER: the puddle dries up
LOCATION: Meadow path (puddle in the dip)
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: puddle, gone, dry, smaller, days, sun, warm, evaporate, less, crack, mud, same place, compare
CAUSE_EFFECT: heat and sun → water evaporates; puddle shrinks then disappears
SEED: After the last rain the puddle was big enough to jump. Two days later it is smaller. A day after that, just a damp patch. The day after that, cracked earth — and nothing.
NOTES: Multi-day observation. The puddle's disappearance is gradual and complete. No explanation of evaporation is needed — the daily observation is enough.

STORY: 117
CLUSTER: why the soup is hot
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: fire, pot, hot, careful, warm, transfer, handle, heat, travel, iron, too hot, touch, test
CAUSE_EFFECT: fire heats iron pot → pot heats soup → heat travels to handle
SEED: Gran warns Emma about the handle. Emma touches it quickly with one finger. Hot. Not the soup — the handle. Gran says: the heat travels through iron. The pot has been on the fire. Emma tests the lid next, which is even hotter.
NOTES: Heat transfer through material. Gran's explanation is brief and factual. Emma's testing after being warned is character consistency (she needs to verify).

STORY: 118
CLUSTER: Biscuit notices first
LOCATION: Meadow path + Gran's field
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T B
KEY WORDS: ears, nose, before, notice, something, there, sound, smell, look, direction, already, ahead, alert
CAUSE_EFFECT: Biscuit's senses detect something before human senses do → his behaviour is the first signal
SEED: Biscuit stops before the children hear anything. His ears go up; he faces a particular direction. Then Emma hears it — something in the hedge, quiet and quick. Biscuit already knew.
NOTES: The dog's senses are the cause-effect chain: stimulus detected → behaviour change → children notice the behaviour → then they detect the stimulus. Observation-dependent: Biscuit's reaction is the evidence for the hidden state.

STORY: 119
CLUSTER: why bread rises
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: dough, rise, bigger, yeast, warm, covered, wait, before, after, same bowl, doubled, poke, spring back
CAUSE_EFFECT: yeast in warm dough → dough expands over time
SEED: Gran covers the bowl and says: wait and watch. An hour later the dough has pushed the cloth up. Emma pokes it — it springs back slowly. Gran says it is alive, in a manner of speaking.
NOTES: The cause (yeast, warmth) is named loosely by Gran ("alive, in a manner of speaking") but not explained scientifically. The observation is the main content.

STORY: 120
CLUSTER: the apple falls because it is ready
LOCATION: Gran's garden (apple tree)
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: fall, windfall, ripe, ready, weight, stem, hold, let go, ready, ground, thud, bruise, not shaken
CAUSE_EFFECT: ripeness weakens the stem → the apple falls under its own weight without being shaken
SEED: An apple falls while they are standing there — no wind, no shaking, just a thud in the grass. Gran says: it was ready. The stem lets go when the apple is heavy enough. Emma looks at the apple and then up at the branch.
NOTES: Cause-effect in a natural process: readiness → weight → fall. The apple was not pushed. Gran's explanation is brief. Emma's looking up at the branch is the moment of connection.

STORY: 121
CLUSTER: sound fades with distance
LOCATION: Gran's field (Taro at one end, Emma at the other)
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: shout, far, faint, hear, distance, carry, word, almost, can't make out, walk closer, louder, clear
CAUSE_EFFECT: distance attenuates sound → voice that is clear nearby becomes unclear far away
SEED: Taro is at the far end of the field. He shouts something. Emma can hear there is a word but not what it is. She walks toward him. The word becomes clearer as she gets closer. By the time she can hear it, she is already there.
NOTES: The cause-effect is spatial-temporal: the closer she gets, the clearer the sound. The discovery of what Taro said happens at the moment of arrival.

STORY: 122
CLUSTER: warm air from the oven
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen (when oven door opens)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: oven, open, heat, out, hit, face, wave, warm, close again, gone, smell, immediate, rush
CAUSE_EFFECT: sealed hot air released when door opens → wave of warmth and smell moves outward
SEED: Gran opens the oven. The heat comes out in a wave — Emma feels it on her face before she smells the bread. Gran closes it again. The warmth stays in the room a moment and then thins.
NOTES: The wave of heat is the primary observation. It arrives before the smell, then both fade. The sequence within the cause-effect matters: heat first, then smell.

STORY: 123
CLUSTER: why the path is muddy after rain
LOCATION: Meadow path
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: rain, absorb, soft, press, boot, sink, mud, soil, water, wet, squish, stick, edge, deeper
CAUSE_EFFECT: rain → soil absorbs water → ground softens → boots compress soil → mud
SEED: After rain the path at the low point is soft. Emma's boot sinks a little and comes up with mud on the sole. Taro presses the mud with a stick — it yields and then holds the print. The mud remembers what pressed it.
NOTES: "The mud remembers what pressed it" is the key observation — the ground is now a record of what touched it. This is cause-effect made permanent in the material.

STORY: 124
CLUSTER: gravity — what falls and what drifts
LOCATION: Gran's field (under the oak)
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: acorn, leaf, feather, fall, drop, drift, spin, straight, slow, fast, same height, different, gravity
CAUSE_EFFECT: gravity acts on everything, but air resistance varies — different things fall differently from the same height
SEED: Taro drops an acorn and a dry leaf from the same branch at the same time. The acorn goes straight down. The leaf spins and drifts and lands somewhere else entirely. Emma finds a feather and drops it: slower than the leaf.
NOTES: Three objects from the same height, three different paths down. The cause (gravity) is the same; the result varies by air resistance (not named). The experiment is designed by the children, not instructed.

STORY: 125
CLUSTER: floating and sinking at the pond
LOCATION: The Pond (bank)
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T B
KEY WORDS: float, sink, twig, stone, leaf, try, surface, below, predict, guess, wrong, test, observe
CAUSE_EFFECT: density relative to water → some objects float, others sink
SEED: They test objects from the bank. A stone sinks immediately. A twig floats. A large flat leaf — Emma predicts it will sink; it floats, then slowly waterlogged, it sinks. Biscuit watches for a while before he loses interest.
NOTES: The leaf's delayed sinking is the key observation — the prediction is initially wrong, then becomes right over time. The cause (waterlogging) is visible but not named.

STORY: 126
CLUSTER: the window you can see through vs. the curtain you cannot
LOCATION: Gran's house (sitting room)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: window, see through, glass, curtain, lace, blur, shape, light, unclear, through, obstruct, transparency
CAUSE_EFFECT: transparent glass transmits light and image; fabric scatters light → different visibility
SEED: Through the glass, Emma can see the garden clearly. Gran draws the lace curtain. Now she can see light through it — the shape of the apple tree, approximately — but not clearly. Gran says: the light comes through but the picture doesn't.
NOTES: Gran's explanation ("the light comes through but the picture doesn't") is the right level of abstraction for a child. It names the observation without the vocabulary of optics.

STORY: 127
CLUSTER: the cold tap and the hot
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen (sink)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: tap, cold, hot, feel, before, test, quick, finger, careful, one side, other, compare, temperature
CAUSE_EFFECT: different pipes carry water of different temperatures → testing before use is a practical skill
SEED: Emma reaches for the tap. Gran says: feel first. Emma touches the cold one. Then the hot — not burning, but warm. Gran turns them together and the water from the spout is somewhere between.
NOTES: A practical cause-effect skill: test temperature before committing. The blend of hot and cold into warm is a simple mixing result.

STORY: 128
CLUSTER: the fire goes down overnight
LOCATION: Gran's house (sitting room)
SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: fire, logs, ash, morning, cold, glow, ember, overnight, burned, fuel, gone, restart, less, nothing
CAUSE_EFFECT: fire consumes fuel → without new fuel, fire diminishes to ash
SEED: Last night the fire was bright and high. This morning Emma comes down to cold ash and one small orange ember. Gran sets a new log on the ember and blows. The fire comes back very slowly.
NOTES: The fire as a system that requires fuel to persist. The ember that survives is the seed of the next fire. This is cause-effect with a continuity element — something remains.

STORY: 129
CLUSTER: tracks in the mud
LOCATION: Gran's garden + meadow path
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: track, print, mud, who, animal, boot, dog, bird, shape, read, follow, evidence, left by, before
CAUSE_EFFECT: something passed → left marks in soft ground → marks can be read to infer what passed
SEED: After rain, there are tracks in the garden bed. Gran asks: what do you think made those? Emma looks: small, round, three forward toes. Not a boot. Not a dog. A bird, maybe. Gran says: yes, and it came from that direction.
NOTES: Tracks as the result of something that has passed. Gran's follow-up (the direction) shows that the cause-effect chain contains more information than just what made the mark.

STORY: 130
CLUSTER: what happens when you knock the jar
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: knock, edge, wobble, tip, spill, fast, before, catch, too late, already, floor, spread, clean
CAUSE_EFFECT: knock → tip → fall → spill → spread — the chain is fast and irreversible once started
SEED: Taro knocks the jar with his elbow. It teeters. Emma's hand is too slow. The jar tips and the water is on the floor before Gran looks up. The water spreads in every direction immediately.
NOTES: A chain of cause and effect, each link faster than the last. Emma's attempt to intervene fails — once the tipping starts, the rest follows inevitably. No scolding; the clean-up follows.

# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# BLOCK 5: BELLO — TWO-DOG DYNAMICS (131–150)
# Stories building the two-dog world: imitation, competition, difference,
# territory, and Biscuit's gradual ageing.
# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

STORY: 131
CLUSTER: Bello's first walk on the meadow path
LOCATION: Meadow path
SEASON: spring
CHARACTERS: E T B L
KEY WORDS: new, path, sniff, stop, fast, slow, everything, too much, pull, ahead, behind, overwhelm, explore
SEED: Bello has never been on the meadow path. Everything stops him — smells, a sound in the grass, the shape of a puddle. Biscuit trots ahead without looking back. Taro is caught between the two leads.
NOTES: Bello's first experience of the familiar path. For Biscuit: known terrain, no interest. For Bello: every inch is new. Taro is the pivot between them.

STORY: 132
CLUSTER: Biscuit demonstrates fetch; Bello won't let go
LOCATION: Gran's field
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T B L
KEY WORDS: stick, throw, fetch, bring back, drop, won't, tug, grip, hold, trade, again, learn, show, copy
SEED: Taro throws a stick. Biscuit brings it back and drops it exactly. He throws it again and Bello runs after it too. Bello gets there first, but will not drop it. He brings it back but keeps hold. Biscuit sits and watches.
NOTES: Biscuit has learned the rule (drop on return); Bello knows the game but not the social contract (drop it). The contrast is complete without explanation.

STORY: 133
CLUSTER: two dogs and one stick — competition then cooperation
LOCATION: Gran's field
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T B L
KEY WORDS: both, same, pull, tug, grip, together, drag, carry between, release, drop, share, manage
SEED: Both dogs have the same stick at the same time and will not release. They run together with it — Biscuit on one end, Bello on the other — both going in slightly different directions. The stick describes a slow arc across the field.
NOTES: Involuntary cooperation: each is competing but they are moving together. The image of two dogs carrying one stick between them is the whole story.

STORY: 134
CLUSTER: Bello at the squirrel hole
LOCATION: The Oak
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E T B L
KEY WORDS: hole, sniff, dig, scratch, old news, Biscuit, done, Bello, new, find, discover, again, fresh
SEED: Bello finds the squirrel hole at the oak base and goes at it with full intensity — sniffing, pawing, pressing his nose in. Biscuit watches for a moment, then looks away. He has known about that hole for years.
NOTES: The same hole is new to Bello and old news to Biscuit. The contrast in their reactions is the story. Nothing is in the hole.

# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# BLOCK 6: EXTENDED ARITHMETIC (151–175)
# Beyond single-digit addition/subtraction: fair sharing, comparison,
# measurement, multiplication, and ordinal concepts.
# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

STORY: 151
CLUSTER: halving the apple (one whole, two halves)
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: half, cut, two, same, one apple, before, after, together, piece, whole, equal, share
ARITHMETIC: 1 whole = 2 halves
ANSWER: two halves
STATES: Gran says "One apple, two halves. They go back together to make one."
COUNTS: Emma holds both halves up: "One, two. But it is still one apple."
PARAPHRASE: Gran may say "cut in two" or "split in half" — both mean the same thing.
NOTES: Halving as division. The "still one apple" framing is important — the total is preserved even though the physical object is in two pieces.
SEED: Gran cuts an apple in half for them to share. Emma holds both halves together and looks at the line where they meet. Gran says one apple cut in two is still one apple.

STORY: 152
CLUSTER: fair share — two children, four cookies
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: cookies, share, equal, two each, fair, count, same, divide, give out, even, four, two
ARITHMETIC: 4 ÷ 2 = 2
ANSWER: two
STATES: Gran says "Four cookies, two children — two each. That is fair."
COUNTS: Gran puts them out: "One for Emma, one for Taro, one for Emma, one for Taro."
PARAPHRASE: Taro says "two each" rather than "four divided by two."
NOTES: Fair sharing as early division. The alternating distribution (one for Emma, one for Taro) is both a counting method and a fairness strategy.
SEED: Gran has four cookies cooling. Two children. She puts them out one at a time, alternating.

STORY: 153
CLUSTER: uneven share — five berries, two children
LOCATION: Gran's garden (hedgerow)
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: five, two, three, one extra, fair, not quite, remainder, more, less, who gets, odd one out
ARITHMETIC: 5 cannot be shared equally between 2 — remainder of 1
ANSWER: one extra (remainder)
STATES: Taro says "Five between two — two each and one left over."
COUNTS: Gran: "One, two, three, four, five. One extra."
PARAPHRASE: Emma says "someone gets three" or "it doesn't come out even."
NOTES: The remainder concept. Five cannot be halved cleanly. The extra berry is the teaching moment — what do you do with the one that's left?
SEED: Five berries in the bowl, two children. Gran asks how to share them fairly. There is one left after two each.

STORY: 154
CLUSTER: which basket has more
LOCATION: Gran's garden (apple tree)
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: more, fewer, less, which, compare, count, look, guess, then count, right, wrong, more than, fewer than
ARITHMETIC: comparison without an operation — which group is larger
ANSWER: (varies — the count reveals it)
STATES: Gran asks which basket has more without saying the number.
COUNTS: They count both and compare: "This one has seven, that one has five. Seven is more."
PARAPHRASE: Taro says "that one has more" before counting, then confirms or corrects after.
NOTES: Estimation followed by verification. The lesson is that counting resolves the comparison reliably when looking is not enough.
SEED: Two baskets of apples. Gran asks which one has more without counting. They guess, then count to check.

STORY: 155
CLUSTER: heavier or lighter — without a scale

ANSWER: (whichever is heavier — determined in the story)
STATES: Gran says: "Which bag feels heavier? Try both."
COUNTS: Emma holds one bag in each hand — one arm drops slightly lower.
PARAPHRASE: Taro says "this one pulls more."
NOTES: Weight comparison using the body as instrument. The arm that drops is the evidence. No numbers — pure comparison.
SEED: Two bags of flour. Gran asks which weighs more without telling them. Emma holds one in each hand.

STORY: 156
CLUSTER: measuring in steps — how far to the pond
LOCATION: Meadow path + The Pond
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: steps, count, walk, measure, far, how many, Emma, Taro, different, size, stride, result, close
ARITHMETIC: measuring distance by counting steps — same distance, different step sizes → different counts
ANSWER: (Emma gets a higher count than Taro because her steps are smaller)
STATES: Emma says "Sixty-three steps." Taro says "Forty-eight steps." Gran says: "You have different legs."
COUNTS: Both count aloud — their counts diverge after the first few steps.
PARAPHRASE: Gran may say "bigger steps cover more ground."
NOTES: The same distance measured twice gives different numbers. The unit (a step) is not standardised. This teaches that measurement depends on the unit used.
SEED: Emma and Taro count steps to the pond — separately, same distance. Their numbers are different.

STORY: 157
CLUSTER: measuring in arm-spans — the kitchen table
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen
SEASON: any

COUNTS: Emma spreads her arms: "One span. Two spans — and a bit."
PARAPHRASE: Taro says "almost three of mine" (his arm-spans are shorter).
NOTES: Informal measurement using the body. The result varies by person. Gran's "about two" is approximate — teaching that measurement can be approximate and still useful.
SEED: Emma and Taro measure the kitchen table with arm-spans. Gran watches and says the table is about two spans wide — her spans.

STORY: 158
CLUSTER: counting in pairs — Gran's eggs
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen + garden (henhouse)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: pair, two, count by twos, even, nest, bowl, two-by-two, four, six, quicker, arrange, group
ARITHMETIC: counting by twos — 2, 4, 6, 8
ANSWER: (the count varies — whatever number of eggs)
STATES: Gran says "Two, four, six — six eggs. Count by twos: it is quicker."
COUNTS: Gran arranges them in pairs and counts each pair: "Two, four, six."
PARAPHRASE: Emma says "three pairs" — naming the groups rather than the total.
NOTES: Grouping for efficiency — pairing and counting by twos is faster than counting one by one. The connection between "three pairs" and "six" is the bridge.
SEED: Gran counts the eggs by arranging them in pairs. She counts by twos. Emma tries the same.

STORY: 159
CLUSTER: three bags of two — multiplication as repeated addition
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen + garden
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: bag, two, three bags, six, total, same amount, each, add, three times, add again, same
ARITHMETIC: 3 × 2 = 6 (as three groups of two)
ANSWER: six
STATES: Gran says "Two in each bag, three bags — two and two and two. That is six."
COUNTS: Emma counts all of them out: "One, two — three, four — five, six."
PARAPHRASE: Taro says "three lots of two" rather than "three times two."
NOTES: Multiplication introduced as repeated addition. The bags are the grouping structure. No multiplication symbol yet — this is three additions.
SEED: Gran needs to fill three small bags with two apples each. Emma counts the total as she goes.

STORY: 160
CLUSTER: the wrong count — counting again
LOCATION: Gran's garden (apple tree)
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E G

ARITHMETIC: counting error — first count wrong, second count right
ANSWER: (the second count is the one that matches)
STATES: Emma says "Seven." She counts again. "Eight." Gran says: "Count a third time."
COUNTS: Emma counts slowly the third time, touching each apple: "One, two, three, four, five, six, seven, eight."
PARAPHRASE: Gran says "count again" not "you were wrong."
NOTES: The mechanics of accurate counting: losing your place, the value of recounting, touching to keep track. Gran does not say the answer; she asks for a recount.
SEED: Emma counts the apples in the basket and gets the wrong number. Gran asks her to count again.

STORY: 161
CLUSTER: the line at the baker's — ordinal position
LOCATION: The Village (baker's shop)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: first, second, third, queue, line, wait, behind, in front, turn, order, before, after, position
ARITHMETIC: ordinal position — first, second, third in a sequence
ANSWER: (Gran is third — that is their position)
STATES: Taro says "We are third." Gran says: "First, then the old man, then us."
COUNTS: Taro counts the people in front: "One, two. We are third."
PARAPHRASE: Emma says "two people before us."
NOTES: Ordinal vs. cardinal: three people are in the queue; they are third. The first is served; the second moves up; they become second, then first.
SEED: There is a queue at the baker's. Taro counts their position. Two people ahead of them.

STORY: 162
CLUSTER: zero birds on the branch
LOCATION: Gran's garden (apple tree)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: birds, branch, there, then gone, count, zero, none, flew, empty, before, after, still a number
ARITHMETIC: zero as the result of subtraction — birds leave → zero remain
ANSWER: zero
STATES: Gran says "Three birds. Then none. Zero is still a number."
COUNTS: Emma looks at the branch: "One, two, three — then they all flew. Zero."
PARAPHRASE: Emma says "none left" before Gran names it zero.
NOTES: Zero as the result of a process — not an absence from the start, but a depletion to nothing. The branch was occupied; now it is not. Pair with story 45 (zero pears).
SEED: Three birds sit on the apple tree branch. They all fly off at once. Emma counts what is left.

STORY: 163
CLUSTER: which row is longer — visual comparison

CHARACTERS: E T G

COUNTS: Emma counts both rows: "Six and six. The same."
PARAPHRASE: Taro says "the spread-out row looks like more" — then corrects himself.
NOTES: Conservation of number: same count, different arrangement. The spread-out row appears longer/more. Counting resolves the illusion.
SEED: Gran puts six apples in a tight row and six in a spread-out row. She asks which row has more.

STORY: 164

STORY: 165

STORY: 166
CLUSTER: how many more to make ten
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen (table)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T G
KEY WORDS: ten, how many more, need, already, count up, gap, make, reach, get to, from, to, short
ARITHMETIC: 10 - 7 = 3 (complement of ten — how many more are needed)
ANSWER: three
STATES: Gran says "Seven on the table. How many more to make ten?"
COUNTS: Emma counts from seven: "Eight, nine, ten — three more."
PARAPHRASE: Taro says "three short of ten."
NOTES: Complement arithmetic — counting up from the current number to the target. The gap between seven and ten is counted forward, not subtracted.
SEED: Gran needs ten pieces of something. Seven are on the table. She asks Emma how many more are needed.

STORY: 168

STORY: 169
CLUSTER: Taro counts, Emma counts, they agree

STORY: 170
CLUSTER: seven apples, three people — how many left after sharing
LOCATION: Gran's kitchen
SEASON: autumn

STORY: 172
CLUSTER: too many to count easily — the acorns
LOCATION: The Oak
SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E T B
KEY WORDS: many, count, lose place, try, estimate, handful, too many, group, pile, number, big
ARITHMETIC: large counts require grouping strategies — exact count becomes difficult
ANSWER: (approximate — "about forty" or similar; exact number left deliberately unclear)
STATES: Emma says "I lost count at thirty-something." Taro says "More than a hundred under this tree."
COUNTS: Emma tries to count, loses her place, starts again.
PARAPHRASE: Gran (if present) says "more than you can count in an afternoon."
NOTES: The limits of counting: very large numbers are hard to count accurately. Grouping is an implied strategy but the children don't quite get there. Estimation as an alternative to exact count.
SEED: They try to count all the acorns under the oak. There are too many. Emma loses her place twice.

STORY: 173
CLUSTER: bigger numbers — the tiles on the shed roof
LOCATION: Gran's garden (looking up at shed roof)
SEASON: any
CHARACTERS: E T
KEY WORDS: count, row, tiles, many, rows, multiply, lose count, start over, give up, estimate, big number
ARITHMETIC: attempting to count a large array — rows × columns as a strategy
ANSWER: (they don't get a reliable answer — the exercise is the point)
STATES: Taro says "Count the rows and how many in each row. Then you multiply."
COUNTS: Emma counts a row: "Seven." She counts the rows: "...I think eight rows." Then: "Seven rows of seven... that is a lot."
PARAPHRASE: Emma says "too many."
NOTES: Rows-and-columns as an early multiplication strategy. Taro introduces it but the counting is imprecise. The strategy is right even if the execution is messy.
SEED: Emma wonders how many tiles are on the shed roof. Taro suggests counting by rows. It does not go smoothly.

STORY: 174
CLUSTER: double and half — the blanket
LOCATION: Gran's house (sitting room)
SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E G
KEY WORDS: half, fold, double, layer, thick, warm, same blanket, two thicknesses, fold in half, heavier
ARITHMETIC: folding a blanket doubles the thickness; halves the area — same material, different arrangement
ANSWER: twice as thick / half the size
STATES: Gran says "Same blanket — folded in half. Two thicknesses now."
COUNTS: Emma feels the folded blanket: "It is heavier on one side."
PARAPHRASE: Gran says "half the size, twice as warm."
NOTES: Doubling and halving as physical transformation. The material is conserved; only the arrangement changes. This connects to story 151 (half the apple) in a new context.
SEED: Gran folds the blanket in half to make it warmer. Emma notices it is now heavier in one place.

STORY: 175
CLUSTER: the school lesson — subtraction as difference
LOCATION: Schoolyard / Classroom

STATES: Emma says "Three more." The teacher says "Correct — eight minus five is three. The difference."
COUNTS: (not applicable — direct retrieval in the classroom context)
PARAPHRASE: "How many more" (Emma) → "eight minus five" (teacher) → "the difference" (teacher again).
NOTES: Subtraction re-presented as comparison ("how many more") in a classroom context. Connects to story 47 (2+2 as "is"/"equals"/symbol). The teacher bridges vocabulary.

STORY: 221

SEED: Mei shows Taro the sluice lever. It takes both hands to push it open. The water rushes in. The wheel starts turning faster, and the floor begins to tremble.
CAUSE_EFFECT: Pushing the lever opens the sluice — more water hits the wheel — the wheel turns faster — the floor shakes.

STORY: 246

KEY WORDS: joint, tenon, mortise, fit, tap, loose, tight, shave, adjust, dry, correct
SEED: Vern fits a tenon into a mortise. It goes partway and stops. He taps it. It does not go further. He takes it out, shaves a thin piece off one side, tries again. It fits.
CAUSE_EFFECT: The tenon did not fit because it was too thick — Vern removed material from the tenon, not the mortise, so the joint fits without force.

STORY: 282
CLUSTER: the grain decides
LOCATION: Vern's Workshop
SEASON: summer
CHARACTERS: V M E
KEY WORDS: grain, direction, split, plane, smooth, rough, with, against, feel, hand
SEED: Vern hands Mei a block of pine. "Run your hand along it." She does. One way is smooth. The other way is rough. "That is the grain," Vern says. He planes with the smooth direction. The shaving comes off clean.
OBSERVATION_STATE: Wood feels smooth when you run your hand with the grain and rough when you go against it — the plane works the same way.

KEY WORDS: potato, sack, soft, rot, mould, smell, sort, keep, throw, earth, lamp
SEED: Gran sends Taro down to check the potatoes. He opens the hessian sack and reaches inside. One potato is soft and dark in his hand. He brings it up. Gran cuts the bad part off and says the rest is still good. They go through all of them together.
CAUSE_EFFECT: A softening potato indicates rot; the rot can spread if left, so sorting is necessary.

STORY: 423
CLUSTER: what keeps and what doesn't
LOCATION: Root Cellar and Gran's kitchen
SEASON: spring
CHARACTERS: E T G

SEED: Gran opens a jar of beans from last autumn. They look good. Then she cuts open a potato from the sack — it is speckled inside. Emma asks why the beans are still good. Gran says the jar keeps air out. The potato sack lets air in.
CAUSE_EFFECT: Preserving in jars prevents rot; potatoes in a sack spoil faster because air reaches them.

CAUSE_EFFECT: The old handle is broken → Vern selects new wood → he measures and shapes it → the new handle fits. Each step comes from the one before.

SPATIAL_CONCEPT: Footprints in frost — the pressure of a foot changes the frost, leaving a dark mark. Each character leaves a different shape and size of mark. The frost melts first where the sun hits.

SOCIAL_EMOTIONAL_IDENTIFYING_EMOTIONS: Emma's body shows frustration before she names it — shaking hands, red face, tight jaw, silence. She recovers through breathing and trying again.

STORY: 747

CHARACTERS: M E
KEY WORDS: lever, push, pull, wheel, turn, water, sluice, heavy, force, move, grind, stone, stream, open, close
SEED: Mei shows Emma the lever that opens the sluice. Emma pushes. The lever does not move. Mei pushes beside her. Together they lean into it. The lever shifts. Water rushes under the wheel. The wheel begins to turn. Emma feels the force through her hands. She pushed something heavy, and it moved.
CAUSE_EFFECT: Pushing the lever opens the sluice → water flows → the wheel turns. The lever requires force; more force is needed when the water presses against it.

STORY: 750
CLUSTER: vern's magnet

SEASON: autumn
CHARACTERS: E V
KEY WORDS: magnet, nail, sawdust, floor, pull, stick, drop, iron, find, clean, sweep, pick up, together, separate

CAUSE_EFFECT: The magnet pulls iron nails through the sawdust (magnetic force acts at a distance through non-iron material). Freeing the nail requires pulling it sideways to break the magnetic hold — Vern does not lift it straight off.

STORY: 370
CLUSTER: rain on the slope

SEASON: winter
CHARACTERS: E T G

SEED: Rain hits the slope and does not stay. Water runs in thin streams down the path, gathering in the dips, cutting small channels through the mud. Taro's foot slips. Gran says the water is finding its way down. At the bottom it joins the ditch.
CAUSE_EFFECT: Rain on the hill slope → water cannot soak in fast → it runs downhill → it cuts small channels in the earth → it gathers in the lowest places.

STORY: 725
CLUSTER: measuring two pieces of wood

SEASON: spring
CHARACTERS: V E M
KEY WORDS: wood, plank, ruler, mark, measure, longer, shorter, saw, bench, compare, line, eye, hand, fit
SEED: Vern holds two planks side by side. One is longer by a thumb's width. He hands Emma the ruler and she sees the numbers — the second plank stops at a smaller number. He marks the longer one, measures again, and sets the saw against the line.
